Additional\\n96:   // messages may have been sent by Envoy to the management server for the\\n97:   // previous version on the stream prior to this DiscoveryResponse, that were\\n98:   // unprocessed at response send time. The nonce allows the management server\\n99:   // to ignore any further DiscoveryRequests for the previous version until a\\n100:   // DiscoveryRequest bearing the nonce. The nonce is optional and is not\\n101:   // required for non-stream based xDS implementations.\\n102:   string nonce = 5;\\n103: \\n104:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n105:   // The control plane instance that sent the response.\\n106:   core.ControlPlane control_plane = 6;\\n107: }\\n108: \\n109: // DeltaDiscoveryRequest and DeltaDiscoveryResponse are used in a new gRPC\\n110: // endpoint for Delta xDS.\\n111: //\\n112: // With Delta xDS, the DeltaDiscoveryResponses do not need to include a full\\n113: // snapshot of the tracked resources. Instead, DeltaDiscoveryResponses are a\\n114: // diff to the state of a xDS client.\\n115: // In Delta XDS there are per-resource versions, which allow tracking state at\\n116: // the resource granularity.\\n117: // An xDS Delta session is always in the context of a gRPC bidirectional\\n118: // stream. This allows the xDS server to keep track of the state of xDS clients\\n119: // connected to it.\\n120: //\\n121: // In Delta xDS the nonce field is required and used to pair\\n122: // DeltaDiscoveryResponse to a DeltaDiscoveryRequest ACK or NACK.\\n123: // Optionally, a response message level system_version_info is present for\\n124: // debugging purposes only.\\n125: //\\n126: // DeltaDiscoveryRequest plays two independent roles. Any DeltaDiscoveryRequest\\n127: // can be either or both of: [1] informing the server of what resources the\\n128: // client has gained/lost interest in (using resource_names_subscribe and\\n129: // resource_names_unsubscribe), or [2] (N)ACKing an earlier resource update from\\n130: // the server (using response_nonce, with presence of error_detail making it a NACK).\\n131: // Additionally, the first message (for a given type_url) of a reconnected gRPC stream\\n132: // has a third role: informing the server of the resources (and their versions)\\n133: // that the client already possesses, using the initial_resource_versions field.\\n134: //\\n135: // As with state-of-the-world, when multiple resource types are multiplexed (ADS),\\n136: // all requests/acknowledgments/updates are logically walled off by type_url:\\n137: // a Cluster ACK exists in a completely separate world from a prior Route NACK.\\n138: // In particular, initial_resource_versions being sent at the \\\"start\\\" of every\\n139: // gRPC stream actually entails a message for each type_url, each with its own\\n140: // initial_resource_versions.\\n141: // [#next-free-field: 8]\\n142: message \\\"type.googleapis.com/envoy.api.v2.ClusterLoadAssignment\\\".\\n148:   string type_url = 2;\\n149: \\n150:   // DeltaDiscoveryRequests allow the client to add or remove individual\\n151:   // resources to the set of tracked resources in the context of a stream.\\n152:   // All resource names in the resource_names_subscribe list are added to the\\n153:   // set of tracked resources and all resource names in the resource_names_unsubscribe\\n154:   // list are removed from the set of tracked resources.\\n155:   //\\n156:   // *Unlike* state-of-the-world xDS, an empty resource_names_subscribe or\\n157:   // resource_names_unsubscribe list simply means that no resources are to be\\n158:   // added or removed to the resource list.\\n159:   // *Like* state-of-the-world xDS, the server must send updates for all tracked\\n160:   // resources, but can also send updates for resources the client has not subscribed to.\\n161:   //\\n162:   // NOTE: the server must respond with all resources listed in resource_names_subscribe,\\n163:   // even if it believes the client has the most recent version of them. The reason:\\n164:   // the client may have dropped them, but then regained interest before it had a chance\\n165:   // to send the unsubscribe message. See DeltaSubscriptionStateTest.RemoveThenAdd.\\n166:   //\\n167:   // These two fields can be set in any DeltaDiscoveryRequest, including ACKs\\n168:   // and initial_resource_versions.\\n169:   //\\n170:   // A list of Resource names to add to the list of tracked resources.\\n171:   repeated string resource_names_subscribe = 3;\\n172: \\n173:   // A list of Resource names to remove from the list of tracked resources.\\n174:   repeated string resource_names_unsubscribe = 4;\\n175: \\n176:   // Informs the server of the versions of the resources the xDS client knows of, to enable the\\n177:   // client to continue the same logical xDS session even in the face of gRPC stream reconnection.\\n178:   // It will not be populated: [1] in the very first stream of a session, since the client will\\n179:   // not yet have any resources,  [2] in any message after the first in a stream (for a given\\n180:   // type_url), since the server will already be correctly tracking the client's state.\\n181:   // (In ADS, the first message *of each type_url* of a reconnected stream populates this map.)\\n182:   // The map's keys are names of xDS resources known to the xDS client.\\n183:   // The map's values are opaque resource versions.\\n184:   map<string, string> initial_resource_versions = 5;\\n185: \\n186:   // When the DeltaDiscoveryRequest is a ACK or NACK message in response\\n187:   // to a previous DeltaDiscoveryResponse, the response_nonce must be the\\n188:   // nonce in the DeltaDiscoveryResponse.\\n189:   // Otherwise (unlike in DiscoveryRequest) response_nonce must be omitted.\\n190:   string response_nonce = 6;\\n191: \\n192:   // This is populated when the previous :ref:`DiscoveryResponse <envoy_api_msg_DiscoveryResponse>`\\n193:   // failed to update configuration. The *message* field in *error_details*\\n194:   // provides the Envoy internal exception related to the failure.\\n195:   google.rpc.Status error_detail = 7;\\n196: }\\n197: \\n198: // [#next-free-field: 7]\\n199: message DeltaDiscoveryResponse {\\n200:   // The version of the response data (used for debugging).\\n201:   string system_version_info = 1;\\n202: \\n203:   // The response resources. resource names in the resource_names_unsubscribe\\n154:   // list are removed from the set of tracked resources.\\n155:   //\\n156:   // *Unlike* state-of-the-world xDS, an empty state-of-the-world xDS, the server must send updates for all tracked\\n160:   // resources, but can also send updates for resources the client has not subscribed to.\\n161:   //\\n162:   // NOTE: the server must respond with all resources listed in resource_names_subscribe,\\n163:   // even if it believes the client has the most recent version of them. The reason:\\n164:   // the client may have dropped them, but then regained interest before it had a chance\\n165:   // to send the unsubscribe message. See DeltaSubscriptionStateTest.RemoveThenAdd.\\n166:   //\\n167:   // These two fields can be set in any DeltaDiscoveryRequest, including ACKs\\n168:   // and initial_resource_versions.\\n169:   //\\n170:   // A list of Resource names to add to the list of tracked resources.\\n171:   repeated string resource_names_subscribe = 3;\\n172: \\n173:   // A list of Resource names to remove from the list of tracked resources.\\n174:   repeated string resource_names_unsubscribe = 4;\\n175: \\n176:   // Informs the server of the versions of the resources the xDS client knows of, to enable the\\n177:   // client to continue the same logical xDS session even in the face of gRPC stream reconnection.\\n178:   // It will not be populated: [1] in the very first stream of a session, since the client will\\n179:   // not yet have any resources,  [2] in any message after the first in a stream (for a given\\n180:   // type_url), since the server will already be correctly tracking the client's state.\\n181:   // (In ADS, the first message *of each type_url* of a reconnected stream populates this map.)\\n182:   // The map's keys are names of xDS resources known to the xDS client.\\n183:   // The map's values are opaque resource versions.\\n184:   map<string, string> initial_resource_versions = 5;\\n185: \\n186:   // When the DeltaDiscoveryRequest is a ACK or NACK message in response\\n187:   // to a previous DeltaDiscoveryResponse, the response_nonce must be the\\n188:   // nonce in the DeltaDiscoveryResponse.\\n189:   // Otherwise (unlike in DiscoveryRequest) response_nonce must be omitted.\\n190:   string response_nonce = 6;\\n191: \\n192:   // This is populated when the previous :ref:`DiscoveryResponse <envoy_api_msg_DiscoveryResponse>`\\n193:   // failed to update configuration. It is expected that no new request is sent after a\n29:   // response is received until the Envoy instance is ready to ACK/NACK the new\n30:   // configuration. ACK/NACK takes place by returning the new API config version\n31:   // as applied or the previous API config version respectively. Each type_url\n32:   // (see below) has an independent version associated with it.\n33:   string version_info = 1;\n34: \n35:   // The node making the request.\n36:   core.Node node = 2;\n37: \n38:   // List of resources to subscribe to, e.g. list of cluster names or a route\n39:   // configuration name. When set, Envoy is able to\n78:   //   terminate if it detects that configuration is stuck at canary. Consider\n79:   //   this example sequence of updates:\n80:   //   - Management server applies a canary config successfully.\n81:   //   - Management server rolls back to a production config.\n82:   //   - Envoy rejects the new production config.\n83:   //   Since there is no sensible way to continue receiving configuration\n84:   //   updates, Envoy will then terminate and apply production config from a\n85:   //   clean slate.\n86:   // * --dry-run-canary. Additional\n96:   // messages may have been sent by Envoy to the management server for the\n97:   // previous version on the stream prior to this DiscoveryResponse, that were\n98:   // unprocessed at response send time. The nonce allows the management server\n99:   // to ignore any further DiscoveryRequests for the previous version until a\n100:   // DiscoveryRequest bearing the nonce. Instead, DeltaDiscoveryResponses are a\n114: // diff to the state of a xDS client.\n115: // In Delta XDS there are per-resource versions, which allow tracking state at\n116: // the resource granularity.\n117: // An xDS Delta session is always in the context of a gRPC bidirectional\n118: // stream. This allows the xDS server to keep track of the state of xDS clients\n119: // connected to it.\n120: //\n121: // In Delta xDS the nonce field is required and used to pair\n122: // DeltaDiscoveryResponse to a DeltaDiscoveryRequest ACK or NACK.\n123: // Optionally, a response message level system_version_info is present for\n124: // debugging purposes only.\n125: //\n126: // DeltaDiscoveryRequest plays two independent roles. every\n139: // gRPC stream actually entails a message for each type_url, each with its own\n140: // initial_resource_versions.\n141: // [#next-free-field: 8]\n142: message DeltaDiscoveryRequest plane through a gRPC streaming mechanism:\\n\\n## 1. Protocol Definition (Data Plane API)\\n\\nThe control plane and data plane communication is defined in protobuf files in the `data-plane-api` repository. The core message types are defined in `envoy/api/v2/discovery.proto` (legacy v2) and `envoy/service/discovery/v3/discovery.proto` (current v3):\\n- **DiscoveryRequest**: Sent by Envoy to request resources (includes node info, resource names, version info, type_url)\\n- **DiscoveryResponse**: Sent by the control plane with versioned resources, nonce for ACK/NACK\\n- **DeltaDiscoveryRequest/Response**: Incremental variants for efficient partial updates\\n\\nThe **AggregatedDiscoveryService** is defined in `envoy/service/discovery/v2/ads.proto` (v2) and `envoy/service/discovery/v3/ads.proto` (v3), which provides two gRPC RPCs:\\n- **StreamAggregatedResources**: Bidirectional stream for state-of-the-world xDS\\n- **DeltaAggregatedResources**: Bidirectional stream for incremental xDS updates\\n\\n## 2. Control Plane Server (Go Control Plane)\\n\\nThe `go-control-plane` repository provides the server-side implementation:\\n- **envoy/api/v2/discovery.pb.go** and **envoy/service/discovery/v3/discovery.pb.go**: Generated Go protocol buffer bindings\\n- **envoy/service/discovery/v3/ads_grpc.pb.go**: Generated gRPC service stubs with AggregatedDiscoveryServiceServer interface\\n- **pkg/server/v3/server.go**: The actual server implementation that:\\n  - Implements **StreamAggregatedResources()**: Handles incoming gRPC streams from Envoy clients\\n  - Calls **StreamHandler()**: Routes requests to the appropriate xDS handler (sotw, delta, or rest)\\n  - Sends DiscoveryResponse messages back to clients\\n\\n## 3. Data Plane Client (Envoy C++)\\n\\nEnvoy's data plane uses these key components in `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/`:\\n\\n**GrpcSubscriptionImpl** (`grpc_subscription_impl.h`/`.cc`):\\n- Wraps the generic GrpcMux with configuration-specific callbacks\\n- **start()**: Initiates subscription by registering a watch on the GrpcMux\\n- **updateResourceInterest()**: Updates the set of subscribed resources\\n- **onConfigUpdate()**: Callback invoked when the control plane sends DiscoveryResponse\\n- Manages per-resource-type version tracking and statistics\\n\\n**GrpcMuxImpl** (`xds_mux/grpc_mux_impl.h`):\\n- Multiplexes multiple resource types (LDS, CDS, RDS, EDS) onto a single ADS gRPC stream\\n- Maintains a WatchMap tracking all subscribed resources\\n- Batches subscription requests and ACKs them with appropriate nonces\\n- Manages connection state and failover\\n\\n**GrpcStream** (`grpc_stream.h`):\\n- Low-level gRPC stream management\\n- Sends DiscoveryRequest messages (or DeltaDiscoveryRequest for delta xDS)\\n- Receives DiscoveryResponse (or DeltaDiscoveryResponse)\\n- Handles gRPC reconnection and rate limiting\\n\\n**Subscription State Management** (`xds_mux/sotw_subscription_state.h`, `xds_mux/delta_subscription_state.h`):\\n- **SotwSubscriptionState**: Tracks server-sent resources for state-of-the-world xDS\\n- **DeltaSubscriptionState**: Tracks per-resource versions for incremental updates\\n- Generates appropriate DiscoveryRequest messages based on subscriptions and ACKs\\n\\n## Configuration Update Flow\\n\\n1. Envoy subsystems (LDS, CDS, RDS, EDS) create GrpcSubscriptionImpl instances\\n2. When subscription starts, GrpcSubscriptionImpl.start() registers a watch with GrpcMux\\n3. GrpcMux batches all subscriptions and sends an initial DiscoveryRequest over the ADS stream\\n4. Control plane's StreamAggregatedResources() handler (in go-control-plane) receives the request\\n5. Server matches the requested resources and sends back a DiscoveryResponse with versioned resources\\n6. GrpcStream receives the DiscoveryResponse\\n7. Subscription state machine unmarshals the resources and calls GrpcSubscriptionImpl.onConfigUpdate()\\n8. The callback propagates configuration to the target subsystem (e.g., RouteConfigProvider)\\n9. Envoy ACKs by sending a new DiscoveryRequest with the response nonce and matching version_info\\n10. Control plane uses the nonce to correlate the ACK and track configuration acceptance\\n\\nThe mux design allows Envoy to receive multiple resource types over a single gRPC stream while maintaining independent version tracking and ACK/NACK semantics per resource type.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2179,"cache_read_input_tokens":81305,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2179},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"73c057b3-0ac0-4d9b-b7ca-9f9720b6e9f9","uuid":"6aa76d1d-e74f-4d34-a391-83a9863334fd"}
